## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the rate of change of concentration (dA/dt) as a function of time and current concentration in a chemical reaction. This is a classic chemical kinetics problem where the rate law describes how concentration evolves, typically following integer or fractional order kinetics.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': 'Zero-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0', 'scenario': 'Reaction rate independent of concentration, e.g., enzyme-saturated reactions'}
- {'name': 'First-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A', 'scenario': 'Rate proportional to concentration, radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition'}
- {'name': 'Second-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**2', 'scenario': 'Rate proportional to square of concentration, bimolecular reactions'}
- {'name': 'nth-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1', 'scenario': 'General power-law rate expression for non-integer reaction orders'}
- {'name': 'Reversible first-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1', 'scenario': 'First-order forward reaction with reverse reaction approaching equilibrium'}
- {'name': 'Reversible mixed-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2', 'scenario': 'Polynomial rate law combining forward and reverse reactions of different orders'}
- {'name': 'Autocatalytic kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A)', 'scenario': 'Product-catalyzed reaction where B = c1 - A acts as catalyst'}
- {'name': 'Inhibition/saturation kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A / (A + c1)', 'scenario': 'Rate with substrate inhibition or saturation effects'}
- {'name': 'Substrate inhibition kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2)', 'scenario': 'Rate law with substrate inhibition at high concentrations'}
- {'name': 'Time-dependent deactivation first-order', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t)', 'scenario': 'First-order kinetics with catalyst deactivation or time-varying rate constant'}
- {'name': 'Consecutive reaction effective rate', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * exp(c3 * t)', 'scenario': 'Effective rate from coupled consecutive or parallel reactions'}
- {'name': 'Third-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**3', 'scenario': 'Termolecular or trimolecular reaction rate law'}
- {'name': 'Mixed first and second order', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2', 'scenario': 'Parallel first-order and second-order reaction pathways'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative rate constants (c0 < 0) indicate consumption/decay of reactant concentration over time
- Integer power of concentration (A, A**2, A**3) suggests molecularity of the elementary reaction step
- Fractional reaction orders (A**c1 with non-integer c1) suggest complex multi-step mechanisms or heterogeneous catalysis
- Equilibrium approach â†’ rate expression as difference of forward and reverse terms: c0*A^n - c1*A^m or c0*A - c1
- Time-explicit dependence in rate law (e.g., exp(c*t) multiplier) suggests non-elementary mechanism or external forcing
- Rational functions of A suggest enzyme-like or surface-catalyzed mechanisms with adsorption/desorption steps
- Quadratic terms in A (like A*(c-A)) indicate autocatalytic or logistic-type chemical feedback
- If dA/dt depends only on A and not explicitly on t, the system is autonomous and the rate law is a pure function of concentration
